Education News Highlights

Ministry of Education Orders Investigation and Prohibition of Private Excavation of Antiquities 65

The Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Education jointly issued a decree to the Education Bureaus of each province and city to investigate and prohibit the private excavation of antiquities:

According to the report submitted by Zhang Ji, Chairman of the Antiquities Preservation Committee, Li Chengmei, a resident of Jixian County, Henan Province, privately excavated antiquities and sold them to foreigners. Please inform the government of Henan Province and order the County Government to strictly investigate and handle the matter. Please also issue a decree to all provinces to strictly prohibit private excavation. In addition to separately consulting, a copy of the original report is hereby issued to order (the Bureau) (Hall) to comply with the Antiquities Preservation Law and strictly prohibit private excavation to value antiquities. This decree is issued with a copy of the original report. The report is to earnestly request the issuance of a decree to all provinces to prohibit excavation in order to protect antiquities. It was found that in January of this year, the Henan Minbao reported that Li Chengmei, the village director of Shanbiao Village, west of Jixian County, discovered an ancient tomb while excavating a water pond and excavated the tomb, unearthing more than 300 pieces of ancient bronzes, including large and small bronze tripods, bronze helmets, bronze lances, and bronze plates. A major antique dealer privately transported them to Tianjin and sold them to foreigners, earning more than 300,000 yuan. I immediately sent a letter to the Henan Provincial Government, requesting a thorough investigation and handling of the case. On the 26th of last month, I received a reply from the Provincial Government, No. 1013, which stated that the previous large letter was read in the Henan Minbao that Li Chengmei, the village director of Shanbiao Village, Jixian County, excavated a water pond and found 300 ancient bronzes and privately sold them to foreigners, regardless of whether it was true or false. The reply was requested, so Jixian County was ordered to investigate and reply. Now, according to the district chief Zhao Tingqu of the district, it was found that in June of last year, Li Chengmei, the village director of Shanbiao Town, was instructed by the former County Magistrate Zhao Ruhu and commissioned by the Fourth Army and appointed members Cui Shibiao and Wei to supervise the excavation of antiquities within 100 steps of the village's western land. No idlers were allowed to watch. All excavated antiquities were handed over to the members and sent to County Magistrate Zhao for transfer to the Fourth Army. Although Li Chengmei was instructed by the former County Magistrate Zhao to assist, he only belonged to the committee's reception affairs, and it was not known how many antiquities were excavated. He also presented the instruction and a letter given by the former County Magistrate Zhao. Later, Gao Weibin, the director of the Public Security Bureau, also presented the same report from the former County Magistrate. The County Magistrate was still afraid that the investigation was not true, so he again subpoenaed Li Chengmei for interrogation. According to the confession, in June of last year, he was instructed by the former County Magistrate Zhao to be commissioned by the Fourth Army to appoint members Cui and Wei to supervise the excavation and ordered the people to assist. The people hired two or thirty coolies to dig out the objects, which were all handed over by the members to the county government and sent to the Fourth Army. It is not clear whether they were sold to foreigners. There were no scattered small items in the people's homes, and they had not sold any antiquities. The former reason for the order was to place Li Chengmei on bail to await investigation. The investigation situation and the submitted instructions and letters are hereby presented to the Government for examination and approval. Also attached are the original letter and instructions. According to this, in addition to instructing, a copy of the original attachments is sent to the Bureau for investigation and verification. It was found that Article 7 of the Antiquities Preservation Law promulgated by the National Government on June 2, stated that antiquities buried underground and exposed to the surface are all owned by the state. Article 8 also stated that the excavation of antiquities should be carried out by academic institutions directly under the central or local government. The regulations are extremely strict, but in each province, because the eyes and ears of the central government are not available or relying on their special power, there are still cases of private excavation that do not comply with the law. It is thought that the archaeology of our country is still in its infancy, and the underground is rich in wealth. The promotion of our country's thousands of years of historical culture depends entirely on this. If we allow the ignorant to privately excavate, mess up the geological layers, and obliterate historical traces, the loss will be difficult to count. Moreover, the purpose of their excavation is to privately sell antiquities to foreigners in the hope of obtaining heavy capital. One person makes a profit, and the group follows suit. The momentum will not stop until the antiquities of our country are destroyed. The power of the association and what it sees and hears are limited, and it is impossible to prevent it. Dare to present to the department that in addition to the Jixian case this time, the Henan Provincial Government should be ordered to strictly investigate the case and track down the original excavated antiquities and send them to the national cultural institutions for safekeeping. Regarding the private excavation in the future, it is also proposed that the department issue a decree to all provinces to strictly prohibit it as a warning to the past and to be careful in the future. Is it appropriate? I respectfully request the investigation and approval of the Ministry of Education, Antiquities Preservation Committee, Director Zhang Ji, 20.4.7.

A Glimpse of Recent Education in Japan (Correspondent Yang Mang of Xin Sheng Society) 66

The Current State of Chinese Students Studying in Japan

China sends more students to Japan than to any other foreign country. The reasons for this are: (1) the expenses are relatively low and easy to bear; (2) the written language is easier to learn, and the preparatory period is shorter; (3) transportation is convenient, and the journey takes only three or four days. Recently, however, due to the soaring price of gold and the increasing cost of living in Japan, Chinese students studying in Japan generally feel considerable hardship, often facing financial difficulties. Those who rely on government funding seem to find it as unattainable as the mythical Mount Shen, or they repeatedly request funding, but the provincial authorities ignore their requests or even directly reject them, a truly pitiful situation. Since arriving in Japan, the reporter has witnessed four or five students returning home due to a lack of funds to sustain themselves. Yesterday, I accepted an invitation from the Tokyo Middle School Youth Association to give a lecture. After the lecture, I met many Chinese students in Japan and learned in great detail about their situation. The majority are diligent and hardworking in their studies, with some eating only one meal a day, and others filling their hunger with cold bread. This spirit of perseverance and dedication is admirable and praiseworthy. There are also a small number of people who, in their home country, held official positions or military ranks, and who brought their families here to observe or prepare for study, and whose lives are relatively comfortable. As for those who indulge in frivolous pursuits and willingly degenerate, although they are not absent, they are extremely few in number. Currently, there are a total of 3,064 Chinese students studying in Japan (according to the latest survey by the Japan-China Academic Association). The largest number of students are from Guangdong Province, followed by Liaoning Province. The breakdown is as follows:

Guangdong: 563 students; Liaoning: 551 students; Zhejiang: 195 students; Sichuan: 206 students; Hunan: 156 students; Jiangsu: 167 students; Hubei: 135 students; Hebei: 124 students; Anhui: 93 students; Guangxi: 49 students; Shanxi: 37 students; Shandong: 74 students; Jiangxi: 224 students; Heilongjiang: 56 students; Xinjiang: 3 students; Fujian: 165 students; Shaanxi: 38 students; Rehe: 6 students; Jilin: 85 students; Guizhou: 14 students; Gansu: 5 students; Yunnan: 69 students; Suiyuan: 11 students; Mongolia: 4 students. Only Tibet, Qinghai, Chahar, and other places have no students studying abroad. As for their fields of study, the most recent survey lists them as follows: Law: 465 students (Law, Politics, Sociology); Economics: 386 students (Commerce, Economics); Military Science: 339 students (Army); Engineering: 238 students (Electrical, Mechanical, Civil, Mining, Applied Chemistry, Silk); Arts: 232 students (Literature, Education, Religion); Railway Engineering: 143 students (128 students at the Tokyo Railway Bureau Training Institute); Science: 138 students; Medicine: 136 students; Agriculture: 81 students (Agriculture, Forestry, Horticulture); Fine Arts: 51 students; Aviation: 23 students; Music: 13 students; Special Subjects: 6 students; Preparatory School, Preparatory Courses, and Other: 813 students.

The most popular subjects are law and politics, followed by military science and engineering. Whether this phenomenon warrants further investigation is a question to be considered. Most students study in Tokyo, with a total of 2,503 students. Kyoto, Nagasaki, Fukuoka, and Hiroshima are next. However, in Osaka, a highly developed industrial center, there are only 16 Chinese students. This shows that young people in our country have not yet paid enough attention to industrial education.

A Glimpse of Teacher Education in Japan 67

Japanese normal schools are quite developed, with the most famous being the Aoyama Normal School and the Toyoshima Normal School. I spent two and a half days visiting each of them and spoke with the authorities of both schools. My brief notes are as follows: Aoyama Normal School was founded in the ninth year of Meiji and is the oldest normal school in Japan. Principal Hasegawa Otsuhiko and Dean Yamada Ikejiro guided me through the school's facilities, classrooms, and dormitories. The school is divided into: Part 1, a five-year program for graduates of higher elementary schools; Part 2, a two-year program for graduates of middle schools; a specialized course of one year for graduates of normal schools and regular teachers of undergraduate programs; and a training course of three years for regular teachers of ordinary elementary schools and above. Half of the students serve in rural areas and half in urban areas after graduation. The school has 627 students, and their prospects are not bad. The school has special classrooms for history, geography, botany, physics, and chemistry, each with dedicated teachers, which is worth emulating. Students collect and manufacture specimens themselves and emphasize manual work. A workshop is specially set up for students to practice, which is also commendable. Toyoshima Normal School was founded in the 41st year of Meiji. Principal Sakuraba Kenji guided me through all departments and sections. This school is also divided into four parts: Part 1, Part 2, Specialized Course, and Training Course. The school has a total of 585 students. It places special emphasis on practical subjects, especially agriculture, with 3,000 tsubo of farmland for students to practice, divided into experimental areas, which is quite interesting. At the same time, students are sent to rural areas to visit, interview, and interact with farmers. More graduates wish to serve in urban areas than in rural areas. Teachers' salaries must be higher in urban areas to encourage graduates to take on rural teaching positions. The school pays special attention to botany, physics, chemistry, and manual work. The Department of Education pays special attention to psychological testing and career guidance, especially citizenship training and character development. Colleagues asked the authorities of both schools several questions, which are presented below: (Question) Should normal schools and middle schools be established independently or jointly? (Answer) The purposes and policies of the two types of schools are completely different. Normal schools should be established independently. (Question) What are your opinions on the issue of coeducation for boys and girls in secondary schools? (Answer) The national conditions, national character, and social organization of each country are different. In our country, boys and girls can be coeducated in universities and elementary schools, but it seems that the time is not yet ripe for secondary schools. (Question) Does your school pay attention to the service guidance of graduates? (Answer) We pay close attention. We provide guidance on academic knowledge, self-cultivation methods, and research. We especially encourage rural teachers to have more contact with farmers. (Question) What are your opinions on the reform of secondary schools? (Answer) We strongly advocate the reform of the secondary school system. Recently, the Ministry of Education divided secondary schools into two groups so that students can have different paths for further education and employment, and pay attention to production and vocational education, which is especially important. However, we regret that we cannot fully promote vocational schools due to economic limitations. (Question) Are your schools preparing rural teachers and ordinary teachers in the same way? (Answer) The level is the same, but the teaching materials are different. (Question) What are your opinions on the issue of sex education? (Answer) This matter is extremely important. When the opportunity arises, the principal, school doctor, and natural history teacher provide indirect guidance and impart physiological knowledge. (Question) Is the internship period for graduates too short? (Answer) We have also felt this. At present, we hope to reduce the number of students and set up more affiliated elementary schools to give students more opportunities for practice. (Question) What are the recent new trends in education? (Answer) It is best for normal schools to divide into departments in the fifth year so that students can specialize and delve deeper, rather than being broad but not precise, and superficial but not deep. (Question) What methods are used to influence students? (Answer) It is best to have teachers with high moral character take on the duties of moral education so that they can serve as role models and provide intangible influence on personality. After visiting the above schools, I noted several common advantages and present them to the people of our country: (1) All schools emphasize character training, so students absolutely abide by discipline, pursue practical learning, and have the virtues of loyalty and the spirit of self-discipline. (2) All schools spare no expense in paying special attention to botany, physics, chemistry, and other subjects, each with extremely sophisticated experimental equipment, and employ full-time personnel to conduct research and experiments without reservation, including geography and history (3) Special classrooms are set up for teachers to concentrate on research. (3) All schools have manual arts classrooms and woodworking shops to engage in productive work, so that students develop the habit of working and the concept of production from an early age. (4) All schools pay special attention to extracurricular activities to cultivate students' ability to be active and serve the community. (5) All schools pay special attention to military drills (military training) and martial arts such as kendo, judo, and wrestling to continue the spirit of Japanese bushido. (6) They pay close attention to the contact with students' parents and hold various gatherings at any time and place.

Anhui Education Director Li Zhonggong's Humble Refusal 68

The Central Government has reassigned the Education Director of Anhui Province to Li Zhonggong. Li is from Guizhou Province, a graduate of Beijing Law and Politics University, and studied in Japan. He has served as the Secretary-General of the General Headquarters and the Vice Minister of Transportation. He was recently transferred from the Commissioner of the China Merchants Bureau to Anhui. It is now heard that Li has declined the position and plans to go to Beijing in the coming days to express his intention to resign to the Central Government. The date of his arrival in Anhui has not yet been determined.

Local News

The Municipal Community Held Two Grand Ceremonies Yesterday 86

Celebrating the Opening of the National Assembly

Commemorating the Establishment of the Revolutionary Government

Two Proposals Passed

Yesterday morning at nine o'clock, representatives from all sectors of the city gathered at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to celebrate the opening of the National Assembly and the 10th anniversary of the establishment of the Revolutionary Government. Over a thousand people were in attendance. Yu Hongjun, Xiong Shihui, Ye Huijun, Yang Qingyuan, Lu Jingshi, Zhu Yingpeng, and Lin Kecong served as the presidium, with Chen Ming and Zhou Hanmei as recorders. The chairman delivered the opening address, followed by speeches from Yu Hongjun, Ye Huijun, Zhu Yingpeng, Jin Xihan, and others, who elaborated on the significance of the National Assembly and the Revolutionary Government. The details of the general assembly are recorded below:

Assembly Order: (1) Everyone stands at attention. (2) Music is played. (3) The party anthem is sung. (4) The most respectful salute is given to the Party, the national flag, and the portrait of the late Premier. (5) The late Premier's will is respectfully read. (6) A moment of silence is observed. (7) The chairman gives a report. (8) Speeches are delivered. (9) Slogans are shouted. (10) Music is played. (11) The meeting is adjourned.

Chairman's Report: Today's celebration has two meanings: (1) celebrating the opening of the National Assembly; (2) celebrating the anniversary of the Premier's inauguration as Extraordinary President. The National Assembly, which is the unified expectation of the nation, opens today in the capital. It gathers the nation's elite in one place to discuss national affairs, marking the most magnificent and glorious page in Chinese revolutionary history. To create a new society and build a new country, we must first cultivate democratic forces. To cultivate democratic forces, we must first enable the people to understand our Party's doctrine, accept our Party's leadership, and participate in our Party's national revolution. This is why the National Assembly is convened. During the era of the Northern Warlords, China fell into utter chaos. Yuan Shikai, Duan Qirui, Cao Kun, Wu Peifu, and others successively trampled on the Republic of China, exploited the common people, and divided the revolutionary forces of our Party. All the imperialist countries took the opportunity to loot and plunder. Internal and external troubles pressed in, causing the country to fall into a semi-colonial status, and the people were plunged into deep water and scorching fire. The horror of being partitioned like melons and beans, facing national subjugation and racial extinction, was imminent. Thinking of this, one cannot help but feel chilled. At this critical moment of survival, the Premier assumed the office of Extraordinary President in Guangzhou in the tenth year of the Republic (1921), igniting the flame of revolution, advocating resistance against the traitorous government, overthrowing the warlords, and overthrowing imperialism, running around and appealing in the hope of awakening the dead hearts and recalling the almost exhausted national soul. As a result, the atmosphere of revolution permeated the land, and the nation's last breath was extended. After Cao Kun and Wu Peifu were overthrown in the thirteenth year of the Republic (1924), the Premier went north to advocate the convocation of a National Assembly to resolve national issues, but it failed to materialize due to various obstacles. He felt depressed and ended his life. In his will, he clearly showed us (recently advocated opening the National Assembly). The Premier's determination to convene the National Assembly is evident. Since the Premier's passing, the spirit of our Party comrades fighting for the Chinese revolution has not diminished in the slightest due to the Premier's death. On the contrary, we have turned grief into strength and become more vigorous and worked harder. In the autumn of the fifteenth year of the Republic (1926), we swore to begin the Northern Expedition and, within a few months, established Wuhan and swept directly to Jiangsu and Zhejiang. We could have unified the country, convened the National Assembly, and abolished the unequal treaties to comfort the Premier's spirit in heaven. However, the Party and the country faced many misfortunes. The Red Bandits wreaked havoc in the front, and the new warlords successively rebelled in the rear. A hasty convocation would likely not yield good results. Since last autumn, the remaining reactionary forces have gradually been suppressed, the new warlords have been completely eliminated, and the Red Bandits have been driven to the brink of destruction. The Central Government followed the late Premier's teachings and convened the National Assembly. The purpose of the convocation is to make public our Party's doctrine, our Party's program, our Party's important resolutions, our Party's basic propositions on Chinese politics and economy, and the achievements of the years of political tutelage, so that the people of the whole country can understand, support the revolution, and unite their efforts to complete the revolutionary cause. Other key points to be discussed at this meeting include automatically declaring the abolition of unequal treaties, recovering all national concessions, and how to effectively implement the equalization of land ownership and the regulation of capital. This National Assembly will have a very detailed discussion and extremely appropriate solutions on the political and economic aspects of China in the future. Representatives, please wait and see.

Summary of Speeches: (1) Yu Hongjun's speech. (2) Zhu Yingpeng's speech. (3) Ye Huijun's speech, length omitted. The representatives from all sectors completed their speeches and then discussed the proposals, passing two important proposals: (1) telegraphic congratulations on the opening of the National Assembly; (2) telegram to the Shanghai representatives urging them to strive for the abolition of unequal treaties at the assembly.

Telegram of Congratulations on the Opening: To the Presidium and all Representatives of the National Assembly: Looking back since our country's reform, many years have passed, but reactionary elements have been causing trouble from within, and the remaining warlords have successively run rampant, so that politics has not been put on the right track and political tutelage has not been effectively implemented. Speaking of this, it is truly regrettable. Now, fortunately, the rebellious elements have been quelled, and the petty villains have disappeared. The National Government, carrying on the late Premier's will and responding to the demands of the people, resolutely opened the National Assembly in the capital on May 5th, gathering the nation's elite to discuss national affairs together. It is expected that everyone will express their broad opinions and work together to plan for the future, so that politics can be put on the right track and construction can proceed step by step, laying the foundation of the Party and the country on an unshakeable foundation and planting boundless blessings for the people. Hearing this from afar, we are overjoyed. We respectfully send this telegram to express our sincere wishes. We ask for your consideration. The Shanghai community celebrates the opening of the National Assembly and the 10th anniversary of the establishment of the Revolutionary Government.

Telegram to the Representatives: To the Shanghai Representatives to the National Assembly in Nanjing, Wu Kaixian, Hou Dachun, Wang Tingsong, Hu Shuhua, Chen Guansheng, and all gentlemen: The shackles of unequal treaties on our country have lasted for a long time. Sovereignty has been destroyed, industry has been stifled, the people's livelihood has been withered, and the international status has been lost. Our people have been running around and appealing for this, and it has not been a matter of a day or two. However, the imperialists harbor wild ambitions and intend to swallow us up. To this day, unequal treaties have not been abolished, and consular jurisdiction is still being held onto and not released. If this continues, how can freedom and equality be realized? How can the suffering of the people be relieved? Their talk of friendship only reveals their cunning, and world peace will never be possible. Representatives, with your foresight, you have long understood that these unequal treaties should be abolished as soon as possible. We hope that you will uphold your grand opinions and express your righteous arguments at the National Assembly, and solemnly resolve to send a letter to the National Government for serious negotiations, vowing not to rest until the goal is achieved. The more than two million people of this city vow to be the backing for the representatives' efforts and the diplomatic support of the Revolutionary Government. The future of the Party and the country truly depends on this. The Shanghai community celebrates the opening of the National Assembly and the 10th anniversary of the establishment of the Revolutionary Government.

The Minsheng Warship Was Launched Yesterday 87

Over Three Thousand Representatives and Guests Attended

The launching ceremony of the new Minsheng warship of the Ministry of the Navy was held at the Jiangnan Shipyard yesterday. Over three thousand guests and spectators attended. At three o'clock in the afternoon, everyone took their seats. Chen Shaokuan, Vice Minister of the Navy, presided over the ceremony, with Shi Guoxian as the master of ceremonies and Ye Yangmin as the recorder. The ceremony was held as scheduled. Ms. Soong Ailing, wife of Minister of Industry Kong Xiangxi, performed the bottle-breaking ceremony. When the Minsheng was launched, the sound of firecrackers and colorful paper flew together, creating a magnificent scene. The Navy also sent two planes, Jiang Yan and Jiang Hong, to soar in the sky and distribute leaflets. The ceremony was completed at half past four, and photographs were taken before the audience dispersed. The details of the proceedings and the speeches of the representatives are recorded below (the order is from yesterday's newspaper, omitted).

Equipment of the Ceremonial Venue: At the entrance of the shipyard's dock on the south side of the shipyard, there was a signing-in area for guests. After signing in, guests received an order form, a notification to the public, and silk flowers and silk ribbons. A parking area was slightly south. Further south was the ceremonial platform, shaped like an "A." The center was the main platform, with guest platforms on both sides, all decorated with naval flags of various countries and slogans of the Navy and the Municipal Party Department. Refreshments were also provided. The main platform was decorated with the Party flag, the national flag, the late Premier's portrait, and his will, as well as a horizontal plaque that read "The world is for all." The revolutionary cause has not yet succeeded, comrades still need to work hard. On the table were burning sandalwood and the bow of the Minsheng facing inward and the stern facing the Huangpu River. The bottom of the ship was painted red ochre, the middle was moon white, and the top was apricot red, also decorated with naval flags of various countries and pine, cypress, and paper flowers. The bow of the ship was planted with a blue sky and white sun flag, fluttering in the wind. The national flag was also distributed on both sides and white and blue satin ribbons around the champagne bottle. The bottle also

Page 14

Planted with small party and national flags on each side. The ceremonial venue was equipped with the Navy's military band, and was guarded by the shipyard's guard battalion and soldiers from the Chuyou warship.

Participating Representatives: At two o'clock yesterday afternoon, the representatives and guests arrived at the venue one after another. They included Tong Xingbai, Executive Committee Member of the Shanghai Municipal Party Department (representing the Central Party Department); Yang Hu, Military Counselor of the National Government (representing the National Government); Chen Xizeng, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau (representing the Executive Yuan); Xu Jinyuan, Chief of Staff of the Songhu Garrison Command (representing the Headquarters of the Army, Navy, and Air Force); Huang Xuyu (representing the Deputy Commander-in-Chief of the Army, Navy, and Air Force); Chen Shaokuan, Vice Minister of the Navy; Ms. Soong Ailing, wife of Minister Kong Xiangxi; Kong Xiangxi's two sons, Song Ziliang and Song Zi'an; Chen Xunyong, Commander of the Training Squadron; Zeng Yiding, Commander of the Torpedo Fleet; Guo Chengen, Director of the Shanghai Arsenal; Xi Dingmo, representative of the Municipal Government; Wang Xiaolai, representative of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce; Guo Lanting, representative of Zhang Zhijiang; Huang Daolin, representative of the Municipal Public Security Bureau; Creely, Commander of the British Naval Fleet in Shanghai; Shiozawa, Commander of the Japanese Navy; Kitaoka, Japanese Military Attaché; Sauer Wangyuan, Japanese Navy Major; Ouyang Ji, Captain of the Jing'an warship; Li Mengbin, Captain of the Haichou warship; Jia Qin, Captain of the Hua'an warship; Fang Ying, Captain of the Ding'an warship; Meng Xiuchun, Captain of the Datong warship; Qiu Shizhong, Captain of the Chuyou warship; Zeng Guanying, Captain of the Chuqian warship; Shi Guoxian, Captain of the Jiangyuan warship; Yan Shouhua, Captain of the Yongshui warship; Zheng Yaoshu, Captain of the Minquan warship; Cheng Meixian, Captain of the Dakang warship; Gan Lijing, Commander of the Sukei torpedo boat; Ye Yuhe (acting), Commander of the Keisei torpedo boat, and over three thousand guests and spectators.

Launching Circumstances: At three o'clock in the afternoon, Ms. Soong Ailing arrived gracefully with her two sons, Ziliang and Zi'an. The Minsheng warship after launching (photo by China Photography Studio)

Wearing a black leather-collared overcoat, a blue satin yellow-edged cheongsam, and beige-colored shoes and socks, she held a bouquet of fresh flowers. At that moment, the military band played, and the representatives of the Central Government also arrived, and the ceremony began. After the ceremony was held as scheduled, Ms. Soong, holding a bottle of champagne in her right hand, shook the electric bell, and Ms. Soong immediately held the bottle and threw it at the bow of the ship. Champagne splashed everywhere, and the sound of music, applause, firecrackers, and cheers rang out simultaneously. The Minsheng warship slowly launched and sailed into the Huangpu River, with its bow facing north and its stern facing south. When it was launched, the Navy Aviation Department, led by Director Shen Dexie, flew two aircraft, Jiang Yan and Jiang Yuan, circling in the sky and scattering colorful paper slogans, and the Minsheng warship also scattered many slogans, glittering and dazzling.

Chairman's Speech: Chairman Chen Shaokuan delivered an opening speech, roughly saying that today is the anniversary of the establishment of the National Government, the anniversary of the late Premier's assumption of the office of Extraordinary President, and the lady holding the flowers and performing the bottle-breaking ceremony, Ms. Soong Ailing (photo by this newspaper)

The day of the opening of the event, Minsheng was launched today. Minister Yang was unable to attend because he was attending the National Assembly, so Shaokuan reported on his behalf that the Navy's construction of this warship named Minsheng has great significance. Because the Premier's teachings, the Three Principles of the People, are the three elements of people's livelihood, people's rights, and nationalism. At present, bandits along the river and sea have not been completely suppressed, so the element of people's livelihood cannot be said to be completely at peace. Therefore, our Navy is working hard to carry out the Three Principles of the People. In the past three years, five warships have been built, in the hope that in the future, warships named Minsheng will be used to realize the Three Principles of the People and complete the National Revolution.

Representative's Admonitory Speech: (1) Tong Xingbai, Representative of the Central Department, said in his admonitory speech that in the past three or four years, the Navy has launched four or five new warships one after another. The order of construction is based on practical problems. The main focus is on supporting people's rights, followed by people's livelihood, and finally nationalism, in order to complete the Three Principles of the People. Therefore, when the Minquan warship was launched in previous years, at the time when the Party was facing serious adversity, the naval officers and soldiers participated in the war and made great contributions. The focus was on eliminating the warlords' separatism, completing the unification of the central government, concentrating all political power in the Party, and transitioning from the stage of Party rule through political tutelage to people's rights. This is what the past work has been able to do properly. Now that political tutelage has begun, everything should be devoted to construction. The primary focus of construction is people's livelihood. In terms of building people's livelihood, there are both active and passive meanings, which must be complementary. The active aspect is to engage in material construction, and the passive aspect is to engage in the removal of obstacles. Today, the biggest obstacle to people's livelihood is the rampant banditry, which makes the people's livelihood difficult and construction impossible. The Ministry of the Navy needs this, so its construction work focuses on people's livelihood, and the launching of the Minsheng warship today also shows its symbolism. But considering the name, all naval officers and soldiers will also increase their responsibility due to the launching of the Minsheng warship. It is hoped that they can use this meaning to go all out to eliminate the river and sea bandits, and once the obstacles are removed, construction will be easier. The people will live in peace and the people's livelihood will be prosperous. Then, we will enrich our military preparations, consolidate our national defense, and promote the spirit of nationalism, eliminate the strong powers of aggression, and complete the great work of the Party's Three Principles of the People. Today, Xingbai represents the Central Party Department to participate in the grand ceremony, specifically to provide a reminder of its inherent significance, hoping that the naval officers and soldiers will implement it. (1) Yang Xiaotian, representative of the National Government, said in his admonitory speech that he felt very honored to be sent by order of the Chairman of the National Government to participate in today's grand ceremony of the launching of the Minsheng warship. The navy occupies the most important position in the military preparations of any country. Especially in China, because of its long coastline, national defense must have a huge naval force. However, before the fifteenth year of the Republic (1926), because the warlords competed with each other and the political situation was chaotic, and the science was underdeveloped, and the economy was backward, for various reasons, the naval power of this country could not be brought into play. However, since the establishment of the National Government, our Navy has participated in suppressing internal strife and established unprecedented meritorious service. On the one hand, it has used the spirit of construction to create the Minsheng warship, which adds a special color to the naval force of this country. The entrepreneurial spirit and creative spirit of the naval officers and soldiers are truly worthy of our country's admiration. In the future, we will use the spirit of quelling internal strife to defend against foreign aggression, and use the spirit of creating the Minsheng warship to continue to create countless larger warships so that our country's navy can achieve a first-class position in the international arena, expressing the Party's spirit of construction to the world. This is what we fully expect from the naval officers and soldiers, and it is also what the naval officers and soldiers expect from themselves. (1) Chen Xizeng, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, Representative of the Executive Yuan, delivered an admonitory speech: Today, the Minsheng warship is holding a launching ceremony. Xizeng is ordered by Chiang Kai-shek, the President of the National Government's Executive Yuan, to deliver an admonitory speech. The spirit of the National Revolutionary Army lies in the actual strength of carrying out the late Premier's teachings and working hard on the Three Principles of the People. Recently, the naming of the Navy's warships has been based on this purpose. The Minquan warship and the Minsheng warship are hoping that the naval officers and soldiers will take the name to mean to arouse the spirit of revolution and not forget the teachings of the late Premier's National Revolutionary Party. In the past process of the National Revolution, the naval officers and soldiers also made a lot of efforts and glory, but the responsibility of the future work is more important. The naming of the Minsheng warship is of course to prompt the naval officers and soldiers to pay attention to the Principle of People's Livelihood. The work before the National Revolution was to fight against the warlords and all reactionaries. Now that the country is unified and has entered the period of political tutelage from the military government period, it should strive for construction and pay attention to the realization of the Principle of People's Livelihood. Because the target of the Principle of People's Livelihood is capitalist aggression. The day when the Principle of People's Livelihood is realized is the day when capitalist aggression is eliminated. This is not only the duty that naval officers and soldiers should fulfill, but also the only mission of the National Revolutionary Army and the National Government. It is not only what all members of this party belong to, but also what all nationalities oppressed under the capitalist aggression of the world belong to. I hope that all the members of the Minsheng warship and the naval officers and soldiers will work hard in this direction from today onwards, do not forget the naming of the Minsheng warship, do not forget the hard work of the Navy Department in building new warships, and take the late Premier's intention to implement the Three Principles of the People as a pioneer in quelling chaos and stabilizing danger, so that the people can develop industry and commerce and live and work in peace, promote national prestige and complete the construction of the Navy, and lay the foundation of the country on the safety of the rock. This is also what I want to boast about today when I hold the launching ceremony. (1) Xu Jinyuan, Chief of Staff of the Songhu Garrison Command, Representative of the Headquarters of the Army, Navy, and Air Force, said in his admonitory speech that the Minsheng warship was launched today, and today is also the opening day of the National Assembly, so it can be said that everyone will have the same permanent impression afterwards. It is necessary to know that the Navy is indispensable for national defense, guaranteeing territorial waters and maintaining national defense. Although there is an army, it will not be successful without the Navy to help and support it. Moreover, the current maritime ban is greatly opened, and even if the countries do not compete with each other in military preparations, they must rely on a strong navy to protect overseas Chinese and develop overseas trade. Therefore, it cannot be said that it is not the era of the Chinese Navy's renaissance that the Navy can continue to build five warships in this economic difficulty. I only hope that from today onwards, we will continue to work hard with the built warships to complete the revolution and achieve the final success. (1) Huang Xuyu, Representative of the Deputy Commander-in-Chief of the Army, Navy, and Air Force, said in his admonitory speech that the Chinese Navy was originally young, but in the past ten years or so, because of the frequent military affairs, it has made a lot of progress as a result. Today, it can actually build as many as five warships itself, which makes me feel fortunate for the future of the Navy. All the navies of a country are intended by the authorities to build ships and train troops for my ability. In fact, the navy is very important to national defense and people's livelihood, so I always hope that one side will work hard on the revolution and the other will be able to lead the people to reach the step of people's livelihood, and the people will also be able to understand the importance of the navy.

Chairman's Reply: Chairman Chen Shaokuan got up to deliver a reply after each representative had given an admonitory speech, saying that he was grateful for the advice and guidance of the representatives and guests, but that the Navy had built warships such as Minquan and Minsheng in the midst of very difficult economic times. Half of the funds were saved from the Navy. For now, let's not talk about what has been completed, but we can give a brief report on what will be and is being planned to be built. (1) A 3,000-ton warship, which is 300 feet wide, is being planned, which is larger than the Yixian. (2) After the warship is completed, we must continue to build it and plan to order a giant warship from abroad. We have set our minds on working hard on the above-mentioned matters, and we will be able to start construction in about three or four months.

Chen Returns to Beijing: After presiding over the launching ceremony of Minsheng, Chen Shaokuan went to Beijing that evening to continue the inspection because the inspection of the warships had not been completed.

The Shanghai County Government Held a Cornerstone Laying Ceremony Yesterday 88

Over a Thousand People Braved the Rain to Attend

The Shanghai County Government held a cornerstone laying ceremony for the new county seat in Beiqiao Town yesterday morning at 10:00 a.m., coinciding with the day when the late Premier assumed the office of Extraordinary President in Guangzhou and the opening of the National Assembly. In advance, the County Party Department, together with the County Government, took the opportunity to hold a celebration meeting in the town to celebrate and spread the news. At 10:00 a.m., there were dozens of people in attendance, including County Magistrate Yan Shenyu, Director of the Finance Bureau Wang Li, Director of the Construction Bureau Wu Wenhua, Director of the Education Bureau Shi She, Executive Committee members of the County Party Department Jiang Yanchou and Tao Yishan, and local gentry, as well as over a thousand people braving the rain. Committee Member Jiang was elected as chairman. The meeting began at 10:00 a.m. with cannons fired, the flag raised, the Party anthem sung, and a ceremony performed as scheduled. After the chairman reported on the purpose of the meeting, County Magistrate Yan took the stage to give a speech, roughly saying that today is the anniversary of the late Premier's assumption of the office of Extraordinary President, and it is also the opening of the National Assembly and the cornerstone laying ceremony of the new house of the Shanghai County Government. No matter what position we take, we should recognize that it is a day worth celebrating. Our party members and civil servants should be responsible to the Party and the country for part of the task and the spirit of service should be modeled on the late Premier. Since the separation of Shanghai County and the city, there has long been a proposal to move the county seat, but it has been delayed for more than two years. Now it is gradually turning from theory to reality, and we have chosen such an anniversary to hold the cornerstone laying ceremony of the new house. Shanghai County is really small in China, but we who serve in Shanghai County cannot but see it as very large, and we cannot but regard the politics of Shanghai County as a great cause. Political tutelage and autonomy take the county as the unit. Only when each county is good will the Republic of China be good. Today's cornerstone laying is just the first step. In the future, after the relocation, we will have to cheer up and lay a small foundation for the new China. After the speech, he led the attendees to the new house base on the west side of the Hu-Nan long-distance bus route in the town to perform the cornerstone laying ceremony, adding a layer of mud to the ground and erecting a stone tablet on which was written (The cornerstone laying ceremony for the construction of houses by the Shanghai County Government was held on May 5, 20th year of the Republic of China). After the tablet was erected, County Magistrate Yan took a car back to Shanghai, while the people at the meeting continued to perform various entertainment.

The Chinese Industrial Association telegraphs requesting the resumption of Luan coal transportation 89

Shanghai Factories Have No Coal to Burn

Now Forced to Purchase Japanese Coal with Pain

Japanese Coal is Expensive, Causing Significant Losses

The Dispute Between the Railway and the Mine Needs to Be Resolved Urgently

Since the Bei-Ning Railway Bureau and the Kai-Luan Mining Bureau had a misunderstanding that led to the suspension of coal shipments, Shanghai factories have been unable to find a solution for the lack of fuel coal, forcing them to purchase expensive Japanese coal with great distress. The Chinese Industrial Federation, recognizing this, telegraphed the authorities, earnestly requesting them to order the speedy resumption of transportation. The original telegram reads: "To Chairman Chiang of Nanjing, Deputy Commander Zhang, Vice President of the Executive Yuan Song, Minister of Industry Kong, Minister of Railways Sun: The factories affiliated with our association rely heavily on coal from Kai-Luan. Since the dispute between the Tianjin Kai-Luan Mining Bureau and the Bei-Ning Railway Bureau occurred in mid-March of this year and coal shipments were suspended, it has been more than fifty days. Shanghai is a city of numerous factories, and hundreds of thousands of workers depend on them for their livelihoods. If the factories are forced to shut down due to the lack of fuel coal, causing hundreds of thousands of people to lose their jobs overnight, the harm would be unimaginable. Recently, various factories in Shanghai, unable to obtain coal from Kai-Luan, have reluctantly purchased Japanese coal to maintain operations. However, the cost is extremely high, and buyers are struggling to afford it. In terms of price, Kai-Luan No. 1 slack coal sells for eight taels and three mace of silver per ton, while Fushun No. 1 slack coal sells for more than thirteen taels of silver per ton. Kai-Luan No. 2 slack coal sells for seven taels, seven mace, and five fen of silver per ton, while Fushun No. 2 slack coal sells for around twelve taels and six mace of silver per ton. Comparing the two, Japanese coal is four or five taels more expensive per ton than Kai-Luan coal. Factories that consume a lot of coal use five or six thousand tons per month, while those that consume less still need thousands of tons per month. The magnitude of this loss is truly alarming, and the future of industry is on the verge of collapse. Furthermore, according to reports, Kai-Luan is experiencing difficulties in transporting coal by rail, resulting in a large stockpile of goods in the mines. To remedy this temporarily, each mine has been stopping work for two days each week. Given this situation, the resolution between the railway and the mine remains elusive, and the supply of fuel is unlikely to resume in the short term. In the association's view, there is no reason why the dispute between the two parties cannot be resolved. Whether through mediation, litigation, or arbitration, a fair conclusion will eventually be reached. However, both parties are not seeking a speedy resolution, relying instead on suspension of transportation and reduced production. This allows Japanese merchants to exploit our resources and causes losses to our industry. Who will bear this responsibility? We humbly request that your esteemed (office) (department) order the speedy resumption of transportation and work in the mines. At the same time, the relevant authorities should investigate the points of contention between the two parties and resolve them swiftly to alleviate the distress of the people. This is a sincere plea. We respectfully await your consideration. The Chinese Industrial Federation bows in respect."

Chen Mingshu's Representative Sun Xiwen Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday by Telegram 90

To Report to the Central Government in Nanjing Immediately

Chen Himself May Come to Nanjing Soon

Shigemitsu Went to Nanjing Last Night 92

To Continue Discussing the Issue of Legal Rights

The Japanese Government's Scope of Negotiations on Legal Rights in China 93

Comprises a Total of Seven Items

The Zi Lin Bao reports that after Deputy Envoy Shigemitsu returned to Japan and reported everything to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the Ministry, after careful consideration, broadly agreed on the following scope for Sino-Japanese legal rights negotiations: (1) Regarding the issue of permissibly revoking legal rights, the Japanese government does not object to formal negotiations with the government of the Republic of China, but only to the extent that Japan will enjoy the same privileges, rights, exemptions, or benefits as other related countries. (2) The abolition of consular jurisdiction, whether phased or not, may have adverse consequences for the traditional and cultural relationship between China and Japan. In order to avoid such consequences, Japan is only willing to abolish jurisdiction over civil cases first, as stipulated below, but only after China has implemented new civil laws based on modern judicial concepts and their judicial effectiveness has been recognized as satisfactory by Japan. (3) Regardless of how the jurisdiction over civil cases is decided, Japan will not allow any changes to the current status of the Kwantung Leased Territory, the South Manchurian Railway Zone, and other similar spheres of influence. (4) If civil jurisdiction is abolished, all Japanese residents throughout China should enjoy permanent, complete, and unrestricted rights throughout China, and the Chinese government must accept full responsibility for guaranteeing the welfare of Japanese residents. (5) Japan will consider whether it can agree to abolish criminal jurisdiction in the same way depending on the circumstances after civil jurisdiction is abolished under the aforementioned conditions. (6) However, during the initial negotiations on the abolition of civil jurisdiction, there must be an understanding that foreign nationals must be employed in all Chinese courts for a certain period of time and have the same powers as Chinese judges to jointly hear cases, until the end of this period is agreed upon later. (7) In any case, Japan should enjoy the same treatment as other related countries.

The chairman of this Congress is [missing name] (a well-known Chicago lawyer and current president of the American branch of the International Chamber of Commerce). The Issue of Ordering Postage Stamps from British Merchants 95

The Beiping Printing Bureau's Letter Clarifies the Original Reason to Shanghai Voices

According to a letter from the Beiping Printing Bureau, clarifying the matter of ordering postage stamps from British merchants, it states that according to the contract provisions copied and indicated by the Postal Department, 150 million postage stamps are to be printed annually by British merchants for a term of five years, but can be extended to six to ten years, not a fixed five-year period. Regarding the printing price, it is in accordance with the contract of the British De La Rue Company, which is US$164.95 per million stamps. As for the reason why the Ministry entered into a contract with the British side, it was not due to poor plate molds. The portrait of Chairman Chiang, which the Bureau previously received for engraving, was a photo taken several years ago and did not yet have a beard, and the deadline was extremely tight, so the engravers were not entirely to blame.

The Three Associations Send a Letter to the Unified Tax Bureau 96

Requesting Remedial Measures

The Shanghai Knitting Industry Association, Mercerized Cotton Weaving Industry Association, and Towel Industry Association yesterday sent a letter to the Unified Tax Bureau stating that since the actual collection of the unified tax on cotton yarn, simple weaving factories have been suffering from the complicated procedures of exchanging certificates and obtaining licenses, which has sometimes delayed shipping schedules and caused business losses. Representatives of various associations have repeatedly explained this to your Bureau and requested that you devise remedial measures. Since our associations have similar businesses, we held a joint meeting on the 29th of last month to gather opinions and make a comprehensive request to your Bureau. The results of the meeting are recorded and presented as follows: (1) We request that your Bureau immediately implement the proposed eight articles on the methods for simple weaving factories to produce cotton yarn directly into cotton yarn woven products using taxed cotton yarn and cancel the redundant procedures of exchanging tax-paid certificates or their transfer certificates for factory entry certificates. The blank transfer certificates issued with the tax bureau's seal should be collected by the various trade associations, and the unified tax bureau should instruct one or two staff members to be stationed at each trade association to verify and affix a re-verification seal to facilitate transportation and sales. (2) The tax refund methods for directly woven products transported to areas where the unified tax has not been implemented or exported overseas should be handled in accordance with the established tax refund methods stipulated by the Jianghai Customs (please consult the Customs Administration or the Tax Department for details) or allow the trade associations to collect the tax refund vouchers of their affiliated factories and collect the tax due from the unified tax bureau before distributing it to the factories. (3) Please add columns on the transfer certificate for (cotton yarn count), (name of the original yarn factory), (month), (because the tax on thread spun from 60 count or higher cotton yarn varies monthly according to market prices), and (tax refund due) to be filled in one by one as a basis for tax refunds. The above three points are what our trade hopes to see implemented soon. We respectfully request that your Bureau consider the suffering of merchants and implement these measures.

The National Goods Maintenance Association Asks Chinese People to Pay Attention to the Declaration of Foreign Merchants Establishing Factories in China 97

The China National Goods Maintenance Association is paying close attention to the matter of foreign merchants establishing factories in China. On the 20th of last month, it convened a joint meeting of representatives of national goods factories from various industries, and the details were reported in the newspapers. Yesterday, Standing Committee members Wang Jiean and Wang Xingyi specially instructed the secretariat to draft a declaration to make it clear to compatriots across the country that the economic invasion of China by foreigners is the truth. The original text is recorded below: Compatriots across the country are aware that our country's national goods industry and commerce have long been under the economic invasion and oppression of imperialism, resulting in a weak country and impoverished people who have fallen into a semi-colonial status. Since the national government unified the country and worked hard to govern, all kinds of shackles that harmed the national economy and people's livelihood in the past will be strived to be removed. The sun and moon will shine again to restore the glory of our Chinese nation. As the unequal treaties continue to be revised, the tariff autonomy is recovered, the consular jurisdiction is gradually abolished, and the extraterritorial rights are about to be recovered, we are deeply pleased. Unexpectedly, it has recently been reported that Japan and other countries believe that after China's tariff autonomy, the weapon of political unity to resist the invasion of foreign goods can be enriched, and the national goods industry and commerce can have the hope of prosperity. Therefore, a new invasion strategy has emerged, that is, changing the export of goods to the export of capital, and expanding Japanese enterprises in China as much as possible. They want to move as many factories as possible from Tokyo, Osaka, and other places to Shanghai to avoid the impact of China's protective tariffs. Therefore, they are carrying huge sums of money to set up factories in China, and all kinds of daily necessities in our country are being planned and carried out. They are promoting the establishment of factories to engage in manufacturing. They are also transporting male and female Japanese workers to China to work to kill our Chinese workers. If such a major event that harms our country is allowed to enter our country and set up factories, not only will they become the hosts instead of the guests, but they will also pose a great threat and oppression to our country's industry and commerce. Therefore, we should urgently gather our strength and rise up together to resist it. We must achieve the goal of strict restrictions to prevent imitation and protect the foundation of the country. In addition to sending a special telegram to the National Government and ministries on April 6 this year, requesting them to pay close attention and find ways to prevent this, the association also convened a special joint conference of representatives of national goods factories from various industries on April 20. After research, the following points were decided: A. Requests to the government: (1) Establish special regulations for foreign nationals setting up factories in China, registering, and issuing licenses, and order local government offices to strictly prevent them. (2) For existing foreign-owned factories, order them to register in accordance with the law and levy heavy taxes, such as business tax and dumping tax. (3) Urgently restrict factories that have not been established from being established again. (4) Notify the governments of various countries to instruct merchants of various countries to mark the nationality, product name, trademark, etc. on the goods they sell to China, and not to imitate famous brands to avoid mixing inferior goods with good ones. (5) Urgently negotiate with various countries to instruct merchants of those countries not to transfer workers from those countries to China to avoid hindering the livelihoods of Chinese workers. (6) Encourage domestic industrial manufacturing. (7) Reduce or exempt taxes on national goods. (8) Encourage foreign trade in national goods. B. Please note for national goods industry: (1) Be sure to mark the words "Chinese Merchant" and the factory name, trademark, location, etc. on national goods products. (2) Jointly raise the basic industries. C. Please note for compatriots: (1) Respect the orders of the National Government and implement the promotion of using national goods. Foreign goods should not be used if our country has products of the same kind. (2) Do not sell land or factory bases to foreigners. (3) Chinese merchants must not covet short-term gains and come forward on behalf of foreigners when foreigners come to China to set up factories. The above points are all urgent and essential fundamental measures that must be implemented. In addition to implementing the plan in accordance with the resolution, the association hereby declares earnestly, earnestly requesting compatriots across the country to rise up together and cooperate with one heart to resist this new economic invasion, the tide of national destruction, and maintain the foundation of our Chinese nation. The timing is extremely urgent, and if there is even a slight hesitation, a tragic disaster will appear.

Detectives Were Tricked Twice

The Truth Was Revealed on the Third Time

The Hostage Suffered Greatly in the Bandit's Den

Qian Chaofu, an employee of the Yongfeng Lumber Company in Lujiabang, Bund, Nanshi, and a native of Anting, was kidnapped along with his car No. 1797 (City No. 1993) at 0:15 in the morning of the 15th of last month from his concubine Yue'e's residence at No. 27 Hehefang, Xiafei Road, French Concession, when his car arrived at the corner of Pushi Road and Saposai Road. The details have been reported in this newspaper. Now, it is reported that Qian was rescued from danger by the French Concession Police yesterday, and four bandits were arrested. The details are as follows:

Negotiations Scheduled, Qian's family was panicked when they heard the news on the day Qian was kidnapped. At the same time, the French Concession Police sent out detectives, hoping to solve the case in the shortest possible time. But the bandits were very cunning and cunning, sending a total of three letters to Qian's house. The first letter demanded more than ten thousand dollars. The family did not reply because the ransom was too high. A few days later, they received a second letter, scheduling a meeting at Room 420 on the fourth floor of the Central Hotel at the intersection of Hubei Road and Guangdong Road in the Public Concession. Qian's family sent someone on time.

Demanded 30,000 Yuan, Arrived at 420, But There Was No One in the Room. According to the waiter, the guest in Room 402 had gone out and asked them to wait if anyone came to visit. The person in charge of Qian's family sat quietly and waited for a long time. Suddenly, a phone call came, and the person in charge was contacted. The bandits said that the minimum amount was 30,000 yuan. The two sides negotiated repeatedly, but there was no result, and they dispersed.

Detectives in Disguise After this negotiation failed to reach an agreement, the news disappeared. It was not until the 1st of this month that Qian's family received a third letter, scheduling a meeting near Daxilu Road in Huxi at 3:00 PM on the 3rd, and the person sent must hold a wine bottle as a sign. Qian's family could not bear it any longer and reported the three letters to the French Concession Police. Chief Detective Bardi, supervised by Chief Cai Jinjiu, Detective Li Yaolong, Deputy Detective Qian Yumin, Zhang Ziying, Mao Jingen, and detectives Qin Youyu and others, disguised themselves as various peddlers and secretly waited nearby. Two bandits were arrested. The person in charge of Qian's family walked to Daxilu Road at the scheduled time, holding a wine bottle on the sidewalk. At the same time, disguised detectives had already been ambushed. At about 3:00 PM, two people, one in a Zhongshan suit and one in a long serge robe, came from the east. The two walked and talked, and their attitude was natural. They first paid attention to the surroundings for a week, then walked past the person in charge and went straight west. After a while, they turned back and asked the person in charge. Before they could say a few words, the ambush soldiers came out from all sides, and the two bandits surrendered.

The Hostage in Chuansha, after the two bandits were brought to the police station, the one in the Zhongshan suit confessed his name as Gu Defu, and the one in the long serge robe confessed his name as Lu Andiang. They said that the hostage was now hidden in a rural area more than 50 miles away from Chuansha. They immediately stated the route. Detective Bardi of the Brazilian police supervised the entire team of detectives and took a ferry across the river at about 6:00 PM that night. They walked all night to Chuansha. The moonlight was dim, and the road was rugged and difficult to distinguish. When they arrived at their destination, they searched almost everywhere, but there was no trace.

Rushing to Minhang, the detectives trekked until night, disappointed and returned. They interrogated the two bandits severely again. Unexpectedly, the two bandits were very cunning and falsely confessed for the second time that the hostage was hidden in Ruoqiao, Minhang. The detectives believed it to be true and went to Minhang again without stopping. They were still frustrated and returned to Shanghai. The detectives hated the bandits to the bone. After the third interrogation, the two bandits confessed the real address. The hostage was actually hidden in a flat upstairs building far away from the police station in Saposai Road.

The hostage was rescued early in the morning yesterday. Chief Detective Ba, supervised by the detectives, took the two bandits to the location they confessed and identified the house. The detectives rushed in and went straight to the loft, rescuing the hostage Qian Chaofu. There were still two bandits guarding him. They jumped out of the loft window and tried to escape, but were intercepted by the detectives and taken to the police station. One confessed his name as Gu Er and the other as Lu Er. Then, the hostage recounted the suffering he had endured in the bandit's den. The detectives then escorted him home. Her husband, Mao Nan, was addicted to morphine injections, and even beat her arbitrarily, and her skin was covered with scars. In the 15th year of the Republic of China, he was criminally prosecuted in the local procuratorate. Later, he took his children back to Ningbo for treatment. In the summer of the 18th year, he was persuaded to return and live together by the clan chief. He originally hoped that his conscience would return and that he would correct his mistakes, but after a few days, he was rejected by Cai's mother and son. She had no choice but to return to her mother's house, and it had been two years now. She thought her life was miserable and could only sob and swallow her voice, but the future was bleak, and the lives of her two sons and herself would be impossible to maintain. When she spoke, she was weeping and crying. Patrol Chief Luo sympathized with her plight and temporarily lent her clothes to change into. On the one hand, he notified her family to come to the police station to take her back to avoid any more accidents.

Korean Man Injured by Tram 110

Involved in a Lawsuit Pending Judgment

Korean Chen Anli was passing through the French Concession on Xiahui Road last month when he was knocked down by a tram driven by Shen Asi, a driver of the French Tram Company. The patrolmen arrived and sent Chen to the hospital for treatment, but he had not yet recovered. Yesterday, the police brought all the people involved to the French Concession Hall for questioning. The plaintiff, Chen Anli, was represented by his wife, who hired lawyer Pulaymei, who claimed that the case had been certified by a notary public that the tram driven by the defendant was driving very fast and that its brakes were damaged. Therefore, there was a risk of causing an accident. Since there are many pedestrians on the roads in Shanghai, the defendant tram company should not have driven the damaged tram on the road. The responsibility should be borne by the defendant company. In addition to requesting an investigation according to law, he also filed a private lawsuit to recover the losses. The defendant was represented by lawyer Bahe, who claimed that the defendant company had full-time car repair workers who repaired the vehicles as soon as they were damaged. There was no reason to drive the damaged car on the road. It should be known that the situation on the day of the accident was that the plaintiff was not careful and rushed out from the side road, causing him to be hit. Moreover, there was a traffic control patrolman at the place with a red light signal. Pedestrians and vehicles should have paid attention. The plaintiff was completely to blame and requested a clear investigation. The Chinese and Western officials ordered a consultation and the court would announce the judgment.

Trademark Counterfeiting Crime 111

Sentenced to Three Months' Imprisonment

Chen Zhengcai, the owner of Wanheng Sauce Garden, was found to have counterfeited gasoline lamps produced by the German Qianxin Foreign Company and sold them through the Rihua and Baohua gasoline lamp companies on Guangdong Road. Qianxin recently learned about this and hired lawyer Lin Yingqing to sue Chen Zhengcai and the owners of the two companies, Lao Yinsheng and Chen Xianfang, for counterfeiting trademarks at the Special District Local Court, requesting that they be punished according to law and that they be ordered to compensate for losses. The preliminary trial sentenced the defendants to be innocent. Qianxin was not satisfied and filed an appeal represented by lawyer Lin. The other day, the joint court of the Special Court concluded the trial and announced the judgment, overturning the original judgment and sentencing Chen Zhengcai to three months of imprisonment for the crime of forging a registered trademark with the intention of deceiving others. Lao Yinsheng and Chen Xianfang knew that the goods were counterfeited trademarks and sold them, and were each sentenced to two months of imprisonment, all with a two-year reprieve. The yarn covers were confiscated, and the attached civil suit was transferred to the civil court for trial.

A Visit to the China Soap Company 113

The China Soap Company's main factory on Yangshupu Road, Shanghai East, was built in the 13th year of the Republic of China and expanded in the 18th year. The land it occupies is as large as 150 acres. Facing the Huangpu River, it can easily import approximately 15,000 to 20,000 tons of raw materials each year through this port, which is very advantageous in terms of location. The factory is operated by a British merchant, Mr. Jones, who is the general manager. He is a man of rich experience in the business world. The management within the factory is methodical and well-organized. To the outside world, it adheres to the principle of small profits but quick turnover, so its business is developing day by day. Now, a new soap factory has been added, specially for the manufacture of Lux soap. Merchants and journalists from this city and other cities were specially invited to visit. Mr. Jones, the foreign general manager, and Mr. He Bo, the factory director, led the tour. The factory is large in scale and uses the latest machinery to replace labor, so it can produce 1.5 million boxes of soap each year, and only 300 workers are needed to cope. There are a total of 26 soap pots in the factory, including 20 large pots, each of which can cook 50 tons of soap, and the rest of the small pots, each of which can cook 25 tons. There are ten steam furnaces in the steam room, which burn about 50 to 60 tons of coal every day. The steam required by each cooking pot is supplied by this furnace. There are also printing machines, wooden box nailing machines, and printing machines that can print five sets of colors at the same time. The equipment is complete and is second to none in Shanghai. The soaps currently produced are Lihua Sunlight Soap, Health Medicinal Soap, Lux Soap, Lihua Soap Powder, Xiangmao, Beiji, and Hexing Umbrella brand, etc., especially Sunlight, Xiangmao, and Beiji, which are the best-selling. The main ingredients of the raw materials purchased by the factory, such as vegetable oil and grease oil, are mostly from our country, and the office staff, engineers, chemists, and workers employed are all Chinese. The products produced by the Chinese using our country's raw materials under the supervision of the Chinese are national products. It is said that the treatment of employees and workers is also very good. The company has always adhered to the principle of continuous improvement, so every ton of raw materials purchased is chemically tested, and every box of soap produced is also chemically tested to ensure perfection. Such a large-scale factory, coupled with the spirit of continuous reform and progress, the future development is limitless.

Lawyer Jin prepared a letter and returned it. Since the tenants organized the Tenants' Union, they have filmed the regulations for cracking down on sub-leasing issued by the former French Consul General Wei Lide (now the Minister to China) into Chinese and Western films, and printed various statistics on the small rent of the neighborhood housing, the interest rate table of the Shangyi Company's rent collection, and the neighborhood housing fund survey table for reference during negotiations.

Recent Situation of Tianyuan Electrochemical Plant 119

Chemical expert Wu Yun Chu, in view of the fact that basic industrial raw materials such as acids, alkalis, and bleaching powder are all controlled by the British and Japanese, gathered comrades to establish the Tianyuan Electrochemical Plant on Bailinan Road, Shanghai West, using the latest electrolytic method to manufacture hydrochloric acid, caustic soda, and bleaching powder, etc., which is the pioneer of electrical chemistry in our country. Its products, such as the purity of hydrochloric acid, absolutely do not contain impurities such as sulfur, etc., are the most valuable raw materials for food manufacturing, pharmaceuticals, refining, and silkworm breeding improvement. Caustic soda is used by local factories in this city, so in addition to supplying solid forms for foreign needs, liquid solutions are transported. The test certificates of the Central Industrial Testing Institute, the China Industrial Chemistry Research Institute, the Shanghai Special Municipal Social Affairs Bureau Industrial Goods Testing Institute, and the Shanghai Chemical Testing Room can be used as evidence. Since the shipment, buyers have flocked to the company from Hong Kong and Guangdong in the south to Liaoning in the north. There is a trend of demand exceeding supply, and on the one hand, mechanical equipment is being added and factory buildings are being expanded. In addition to the original factory director Shen Yizhu and general engineer Bai Nuya, Yu Xueyang has been hired as an engineer to preside over general affairs. Mr. Yu graduated from the graduate school of the University of Michigan in the United States with a master's degree and served as a chemist in the Aohai River Paper Mill in the United States and the director of the research department of the Wuzhou Guben Soap and Pharmaceutical Factory for many years after returning to China. He has rich experience and learning. The year before last, he served as a representative of the Chinese Engineering Society to attend the International Industrial Conference in Tokyo. Last year, he returned from Japan and was invited by the Agricultural College of Zhejiang University, but he did not take the position and was willing to devote himself to the lifeblood of China's emerging basic industry, so the future development can be celebrated even more for Tianyuan.

Yuanchangxiang and Yongchangxiang Bankrupt

Yuanchangxiang and Yongchangxiang department stores, located at the west end of Shengliping Alley on Gongguan Road, French Concession, were founded by Zhu Caiyuan and have been around for several years. Last year, when the Yongchangxiang store site was subleased to Meifeng to open a silk satin shop, the store was merged into Yongyuanxiang in Shengliping Alley. Now, because Meifeng Silk Bureau is expanding its plan and moving Meifeng to the west end of Yuqingli, the house has been returned to the sub-lessor, so Zhu Caiyuan redecorated the vacant house, tied up lights, and relaunched Yongchangxiang, and posted slogans commemorating the fifth anniversary of the big sale, and tied up the drama of the iron bow chicken on the gate tower of the store gate. The tied up paper and silk figures are automatically wired to attract the attention of passers-by. This is to attract customers, so business has been quite good for several days. It is said that Zhu used the revolving funds for speculation and failed, and hired accountants Pan Qibang and Wu Zheng and lawyer Fei Xizhen to draw up a joint notice. Yesterday morning, the two stores suddenly went bankrupt at the same time. A liquidation notice was posted on the door, limiting creditors to open their debts within 14 days and send them to the two accountants Pan and Wu for presentation to the public office for review and handling. The creditors received this news, saying that Zhu Caiyuan used the name of the new opening as a big sale, collected the existing funds from the inventory, and then disappeared and did not meet them. The creditors all gathered at the store at about 11:00 am to discuss the countermeasures. Because the creditors have not yet gathered, it was decided to hold a general meeting of creditors today before discussing the repayment measures.
